## Appendix A - The Children's Portfolio: For Mila and Malou

This book ends with a letter to my granddaughter Mila. But a letter isn't enough. If I believe in the world described in the preceding chapters — and I do — then I must act on it. For the two people it matters most to.

Mila is three. Malou will be born in April 2026. When they turn eighteen — in 2041 and 2044 — the machine economy will be reality. Not as a thesis, but as everyday life.

The question: how do I give my grandchildren the best possible financial start in this world?

The answer: a monthly savings plan that applies this book's barbell logic to a child's horizon of 15 to 18 years.

### The Custodial Account

For children in the US, there are several options for investment accounts:

**529 Plans:** Tax-advantaged education savings accounts. Contributions grow tax-free and withdrawals for qualified education expenses (tuition, room, board, books) are tax-free. Since the SECURE 2.0 Act, unused 529 funds can be rolled into a Roth IRA (up to $35,000 lifetime limit) after the account has been open 15 years. Each state offers its own plan — many allow any state's residents to invest. Top plans: Utah my529, Nevada Vanguard, New York 529.

**UGMA/UTMA Custodial Accounts:** Uniform Gifts/Transfers to Minors Act accounts. More flexible than 529s — no restriction to education expenses. The account is in the child's name, managed by a custodian (parent/grandparent), and transfers to the child at age 18 or 21 (depending on state). Can hold stocks, ETFs, bonds, and in some cases crypto. Downside: the "kiddie tax" — unearned income above $2,500 is taxed at the parent's rate.

**Coverdell ESA (Education Savings Account):** $2,000 annual contribution limit. Grows tax-free for education expenses. More investment flexibility than most 529 plans but lower contribution limits.

**Roth IRA for Kids:** If the child has earned income (from a family business, modeling, acting), you can open a Roth IRA. Contributions up to $7,000 (2026) or earned income, whichever is less. Tax-free growth for life — arguably the most powerful account for a young person.

As a grandparent, I set up the UGMA/UTMA through the child's parents and transfer the monthly contribution. For education-specific saving, I complement with a 529.

### The AI Species Children's Barbell

With a 15- to 18-year horizon, you can invest more aggressively than in an adult portfolio. Corrections and crashes have plenty of time to recover.

#### Variant A — The Simple Way (1 ETF)

| Asset | Product / Ticker | Share | Amount |
|-------|-----------------|-------|--------|
| S&P 500 ETF | VOO | 100% | $200 |

*$200 per month into an S&P 500 ETF (Vanguard VOO, expense ratio: 0.03%) or a Total World Stock ETF (Vanguard VT, expense ratio: 0.07%). Historically 7–9% returns per year. At 8% over 18 years: roughly $96,000 (invested: $43,200).*

#### Variant B — With AI Tilt (3 ETFs)

| Asset | Product / Ticker | Share | Amount |
|-------|-----------------|-------|--------|
| S&P 500 ETF | VOO | 60% | $120 |
| Nasdaq-100 ETF | QQQ | 25% | $50 |
| Robotics ETF | BOTZ | 15% | $30 |
| **Total** | | **100%** | **$200** |

*60% S&P 500 ($120), 25% Nasdaq-100 ($50, ticker: QQQ), 15% Robotics ETF ($30, ticker: BOTZ). At 10% return: roughly $120,000 after 18 years.*

#### Variant C — The Aggressive Children's Barbell

| Asset | Product / Ticker | Share | Amount |
|-------|-----------------|-------|--------|
| S&P 500 ETF | VOO | 50% | $100 |
| Nasdaq-100 ETF | QQQ | 20% | $40 |
| Robotics ETF | BOTZ | 10% | $20 |
| Bitcoin* | In own account | 15% | $30 |
| Ethereum* | In own account | 5% | $10 |
| **Total** | | **100%** | **$200** |

*50% S&P 500 ($100), 20% Nasdaq-100 ($40), 10% Robotics ETF ($20), 15% Bitcoin ($30), 5% Ethereum ($10). Crypto can't be held directly in a UGMA/UTMA in most cases — I buy that portion in my own name and transfer at the 18th birthday. At conservatively estimated returns: roughly $141,000. With optimistic crypto development: up to $195,000.*

### The Tax Strategy

**529 Plans:** Contributions aren't federally tax-deductible, but many states offer state tax deductions. Growth and qualified withdrawals are tax-free. The SECURE 2.0 Roth IRA rollover option adds flexibility.

**UGMA/UTMA:** First $1,300 of unearned income is tax-free. Next $1,300 taxed at the child's rate. Above $2,600 taxed at the parent's marginal rate ("kiddie tax"). Once the child turns 19 (or 24 if a full-time student), all income is taxed at their own rate.

**Crypto held in your name:** Subject to your own capital gains rates. For gifting to grandchildren: the annual gift tax exclusion is $18,000 per recipient (2026). The lifetime gift tax exemption is $13.61 million. At the amounts we're discussing, gift tax isn't a concern.

**Long-term capital gains:** Hold Bitcoin and Ethereum for more than a year before gifting or selling. Long-term rates (0/15/20%) are far better than short-term (ordinary income rates).

### What I Choose for Mila and Malou

Variant C. $200 per month per child. $400 total.

The reason: Mila and Malou have 15 to 18 years. That's long enough to survive the next crypto winter, the next tech crash, and the next bear market. And long enough to benefit from the machine economy described in this book.

If I'm right, they'll have a portfolio at eighteen that gives them a start in life most of their peers won't have. And if I'm wrong? Then they still have a broadly diversified ETF portfolio that will almost certainly be in the black after 18 years.

That's the barbell. Limited risk. Unlimited upside. For the two innocent young people being born into a future that, without their own portfolio, won't give them a chance at a self-determined life.

## Appendix B - Glossary

The most important terms from the worlds of crypto, blockchain, and artificial intelligence — explained for people who know how a bank works but not how a blockchain ticks.

**AGI (Artificial General Intelligence):** An AI that can do everything a human can — think, learn, solve problems, be creative. This doesn't exist yet; current AI is more like a highly specialized clerk who masters only one task. AGI would be the generalist who could staff every window in the bank.

**Alignment:** The art of teaching an AI to do what humans actually want. And not just what you literally told it. Imagine a new intern who follows instructions to the letter instead of understanding the intent behind them. Alignment ensures the AI understands the intent.

**Autonomous Agent:** An AI program that independently handles tasks, makes decisions, and executes actions without a human approving every step. Like a portfolio manager with full discretionary authority who buys and sells on their own, instead of calling for every transaction.

**BCI (Brain-Computer Interface):** A direct connection between brain and computer. Instead of keyboard or mouse, you control devices with your thoughts. Sounds like science fiction but is already being used with paralyzed patients.

**Bitcoin:** The first and best-known cryptocurrency — digital money without a central bank. Think of gold that exists only digitally: limited to 21 million units, unforgeable, and transferable worldwide without a bank in between.

**Blockchain:** A digital ledger stored simultaneously on thousands of computers. Each new page (block) is chained to the previous one and can't be altered after the fact. As if every branch of a bank kept the same ledger. And every entry were carved in stone.

**Bridge:** A technical bridge between two different blockchains. Since blockchains normally can't talk to each other, a bridge is like a currency exchange counter at the airport: you swap your tokens from one network into another.

**CBDC (Central Bank Digital Currency):** Digital central bank money — like the digital dollar the Federal Reserve is exploring. Unlike Bitcoin, a CBDC is issued and controlled by the central bank. Essentially your checking account balance, but held directly at the central bank instead of your commercial bank.

**Cold Storage:** The safest way to store cryptocurrencies — on a device not connected to the internet. Like a safe deposit box in the vault: nobody can reach it online; you have to physically go there.

**DAO (Decentralized Autonomous Organization):** An organization governed by its members through voting, without a board of directors or CEO. The rules are written in software. Like a cooperative whose bylaws execute automatically.

**DApp (Decentralized Application):** An app that doesn't run on a single server but on a blockchain. No company can shut it down; no admin can delete your data. Imagine online banking that no bank owns.

**DeFi (Decentralized Finance):** Financial services without a bank. Instead of a bank managing your loan, a computer program on a blockchain does it. Same function, no middlemen.

**DePIN (Decentralized Physical Infrastructure Networks):** Real infrastructure — like WiFi hotspots, weather stations, or storage space — operated by a community instead of a corporation. Each participant provides hardware and gets paid in tokens.

**Digital Twin:** A digital copy of a real object or process. Your bank has an IT system mapping all accounts — a digital twin of an entire factory or city goes further: it simulates reality in real time.

**ETP/ETN (Exchange Traded Product / Exchange Traded Note):** Exchange-traded securities that track the price of cryptocurrencies without you having to buy and custody Bitcoin yourself. Like a gold ETC: you don't own the bar, but you benefit from the gold price.

**Ethereum:** The second-largest blockchain after Bitcoin, but with a crucial difference: programs (smart contracts) run on Ethereum. If Bitcoin is digital gold, Ethereum is a programmable world computer on which entire financial systems can be built.

**Foundation Model:** A massive AI model trained on enormous amounts of data, serving as the basis for many different applications. Like a generalist with dual degrees who can then specialize in any field.

**Gas Fees:** Transaction fees on a blockchain — especially Ethereum. Every action on the blockchain costs "gas," similar to how every bank wire has a processing fee. During peak times, gas fees surge — like taxi prices during rush hour.

**GPU (Graphics Processing Unit):** Originally developed for computer graphics, GPUs are now the workhorses of AI. They can execute thousands of calculations in parallel — perfect for training large AI models. The GPU shortage is one of the bottlenecks of the AI revolution.

**Hallucination:** When an AI gives convincingly sounding but completely fabricated answers. It doesn't lie intentionally — it "hallucinates" because it continues patterns instead of checking facts. Like a colleague who'd rather invent an answer than say "I don't know."

**Hash Rate:** The computing power a mining network applies, measured in hashes per second. The higher the hash rate, the more secure the network. Like the number of security locks on a vault — more is better.

**Inference:** When an already-trained AI does its job — writing text, recognizing images, making decisions. Training is the education; inference is the workday afterward.

**KYC/AML (Know Your Customer / Anti-Money Laundering):** Identity verification and money laundering prevention — standard in banking. In the crypto world, increasingly the same rules apply: exchanges must know who their customers are.

**Layer-1 / Layer-2:** Layer-1 is the main blockchain (e.g., Ethereum); Layer-2 is a layer on top that makes transactions faster and cheaper. Comparison: Layer-1 is the highway; Layer-2 is the express lane that relieves traffic and feeds back onto the highway.

**LLM (Large Language Model):** The AI models behind ChatGPT and company — trained on massive text volumes to understand and generate human language. Not real thinking, but impressively good pattern recognition. Like an employee who's read every book in the world but still lacks independent judgment.

**Loitering Munition:** Armed drones that circle over an area and can autonomously engage targets. Mentioned in the book as an example of the fusion of AI and military technology.

**MiCA (Markets in Crypto-Assets Regulation):** The EU regulatory framework for crypto assets, in force since 2024. MiCA is to crypto what MiFID II is to securities: a unified European regulatory framework with licensing requirements and consumer protections.

**Mining:** The process where computers solve complex computational tasks to add new blocks to the blockchain and receive cryptocurrency as a reward. Like gold panning — but with electricity instead of a shovel.

**NFT (Non-Fungible Token):** A digital certificate of authenticity on the blockchain — unique and non-interchangeable. Every dollar is the same (fungible), but an NFT is like a numbered art print: there's only this one copy with this number.

**Node:** A computer in the blockchain network that stores a copy of the entire ledger and verifies transactions. More nodes = more decentralized and secure network. Like a branch that independently validates transactions.

**On-Chain:** Everything that happens directly on the blockchain and is stored there, visible to everyone. On-chain data is like notarized entries: public, immutable, verifiable.

**Oracle:** A service that feeds real-world data (stock prices, weather, sports scores) into a blockchain. Blockchains live in their own world and need oracles as windows to the outside. Like a courier bringing the bank current market prices.

**Private Key / Public Key:** Your private key is the password to your crypto wealth — lose it and the money is gone. Forever. The public key is like your account number: everyone can know it so they can send you money. The private key you show to nobody — like your PIN.

**Proof of Work / Proof of Stake:** Two methods blockchains use to secure transactions. Proof of Work (Bitcoin) does it through computing power — energy-intensive like a vault-cracking competition. Proof of Stake (Ethereum since 2022) relies on deposited capital: cheat and you lose your stake. Like a security deposit instead of an exam.

**RWA (Real World Assets):** Real assets — real estate, bonds, gold — represented as tokens on a blockchain. Instead of buying an entire office tower, you own a token representing one-thousandth. Like fund shares, but on the blockchain.

**Self-Custody:** You hold your cryptocurrencies yourself, without a bank or exchange in between. Full control, full responsibility. Like cash in a home safe instead of a bank account: nobody can freeze it, but if you lose it, no helpline can save you.

**Smart Contract:** A program on the blockchain that executes automatically when certain conditions are met. Not a contract in the legal sense — more like a vending machine: money in, condition met, action executed. Like a standing order, but arbitrarily complex.

**SMR (Small Modular Reactor):** Small, modular nuclear reactors — a new generation of nuclear power plants that are smaller, cheaper, and faster to build. Relevant in this book because Bitcoin mining and AI data centers need enormous amounts of power.

**Stablecoin:** A cryptocurrency pegged to a stable value — usually the US dollar. While Bitcoin swings like a roller coaster, a stablecoin stays at about $1. The digital equivalent of a money market fund: boring, but reliable.

**Staking:** You "park" your cryptocurrency in the network to help secure it, and receive interest in return. Like a certificate of deposit: your money works while it's locked up.

**Token:** A digital asset on a blockchain. Can represent anything — money, voting rights, artwork, company shares. Bitcoin is a token, but not every token is Bitcoin. Think of arcade tokens: same shape, different values.

**Tokenization:** The process of converting real assets into digital tokens. A property is divided into 10,000 tokens tradable on a blockchain exchange. Like securitization (ABS), but more transparent and tradable 24/7.

**TVL (Total Value Locked):** The total value of all assets deposited in a DeFi protocol — the most important metric in the DeFi world. Comparable to a bank's total assets: shows how much trust the system commands.

**Wallet:** Your digital wallet for cryptocurrencies. More precisely, a wallet doesn't store the coins themselves but the keys to them. Like a keychain: the valuables are on the blockchain; the wallet opens the door.

**Yield Farming:** A DeFi strategy where you move your cryptocurrencies between different protocols to grab the highest yields. Like hopping between savings accounts for the best rate — but automated and with significantly higher risks.

**Zero-Knowledge Proof:** A cryptographic method that lets you prove something without revealing the information itself. Example: you prove you're over 18 without disclosing your birth date. Relevant for privacy on blockchains.

## Appendix C - Implementation for German Investors

This book describes an investment thesis. This appendix makes it practically actionable — for anyone with a brokerage account at a German online broker. As of: February 2026. Products and ISINs may change. Current information is available on the companion website: TheAiSpecies.world

### The Safe Core: ETFs and Individual Stocks

For the safe core of the barbell portfolio, broadly diversified ETFs tradable on the German Stock Exchange (Xetra):

**Global Tech Exposure:** The Invesco Nasdaq-100 ETF (ISIN: IE00BFZXGZ54) tracks the 100 largest technology stocks. NVIDIA, Microsoft, Apple, Alphabet, Amazon, and Meta are the heaviest positions. Expense ratio: 0.30% per year.

**Broad Market Coverage:** For less tech concentration, choose the iShares MSCI World ETF (ISIN: IE00B4L5Y983). Over 1,500 companies from 23 developed markets. Expense ratio: 0.20%.

**Robotics and Automation:** The iShares Automation & Robotics UCITS ETF (ISIN: IE00BYZK4552) invests specifically in companies benefiting from automation, including NVIDIA, Intuitive Surgical, Keyence, and ABB.

**Energy and Uranium:** The Global X Uranium ETF (ISIN: IE000NDWFGA5) invests in uranium producers and utilities. For the nuclear thesis from Chapter 9, a targeted bet.

### The Asymmetric Side: Crypto Access

**Bitcoin:** The CoinShares Physical Bitcoin ETP (ISIN: GB00BLD4ZL17) and the 21Shares Bitcoin ETP (ISIN: CH0454664001) are tradable on the German Stock Exchange. Physically backed, regulated, purchasable through any brokerage account.

**Ethereum:** The CoinShares Physical Ethereum ETP (ISIN: GB00BLD4ZM24) provides the simplest regulated access.

**Broader Crypto Exposure:** The 21Shares Crypto Basket Index ETP (ISIN: CH0445689208) holds the largest cryptocurrencies by market capitalization — diversification across Bitcoin, Ethereum, and beyond.

For direct crypto investments beyond ETPs: Regulated exchanges like Bitstamp (MiCA license applied for) or Kraken provide access to tokens like OLAS, FET, or RENDER. Note the tax implications: cryptocurrencies held for more than one year are tax-free in Germany under current law. For shorter holding periods, your personal income tax rate applies.

[!] Important Notice

This book is not investment advice. The products mentioned serve as illustrations, not recommendations. Every investment decision should be based on your own risk tolerance, financial situation, and ideally the counsel of a licensed financial advisor.

## Appendix D - Tokenomics Comparison

The following tokens are mentioned in the book as examples of machine economy infrastructure. This overview provides a snapshot of the most important metrics. As of: February 2026.

**OLAS (Autonolas):** Governance token for autonomous AI agents. Total supply fixed at 526 million tokens, roughly 60% in circulation at time of writing. Staking available with variable yields. Utility: governance over the Olas protocol, which coordinates autonomous agent services. Inflation rate declining through token burns on protocol usage.

**FET (Fetch.ai / ASI Alliance):** Infrastructure token for AI agents. Total supply 2.7 billion tokens, practically all in circulation. Part of the Artificial Superintelligence Alliance (merged from Fetch.ai, SingularityNET, and Ocean Protocol). Staking with annual yields around 7–10%. Utility: payment for agent services and compute on the Fetch network.

**RENDER (Render Network):** Token for decentralized GPU rendering. Total supply 531 million tokens. Burn-and-mint mechanism: tokens are burned on usage and new ones minted for GPU providers. No traditional staking. Utility: payment for GPU compute time for 3D rendering, AI training, and inference.

**PEAQ (peaq Network):** Layer-1 blockchain for DePIN (Decentralized Physical Infrastructure Networks). Token in early stage; total supply and unlock schedule still evolving. Staking for network security. Utility: governance and transaction fees for IoT devices and machine-to-machine payments.

## Appendix E - Bibliography

The following overview covers all works cited or referenced in the book, organized by category. Full individual citations appear in the Endnotes.

### Books

### Data Sources and On-Chain Analysis

Artemis (artemis.xyz) - Stablecoin volumes and on-chain transaction data.

Chainalysis / CoinGecko - Stablecoin market data and blockchain analytics.

Crunchbase / PitchBook - Startup funding data, particularly for longevity and AI.

DefiLlama (defillama.com) - TVL data for all DeFi protocols, open source.

Dune Analytics (dune.com) - Custom on-chain dashboards for Ethereum, Solana, and others.

Glassnode (glassnode.com) - Bitcoin and Ethereum on-chain metrics.

rwa.xyz - Specialized data for tokenized real-world assets: TVL, protocol comparisons, growth rates.

The Block (theblock.co) - Research dashboards for crypto market data and institutional flows.

Back Cover

"Artificial intelligence isn't just replacing jobs. It's rewriting the rules of the economy."

Thomas Huhn builds AI products himself, has been investing in stocks since his college days studying business informatics, and in crypto since 2017. For over three decades, he's watched technology waves swallow entire industries. What he sees now is what drove him to write this book.

AI agents that act autonomously. Robots that work in factories and eventually our living rooms. And a crypto infrastructure that enables machines to do what they never could before: pay on their own, sign contracts, conduct business. Three technologies that each change the rules of the game on their own. Together, they create an economy where machines don't just produce — they also consume.

The AI Species is the unfiltered analysis of a practitioner with skin in the game. From the geopolitics of the chip war to AI's insatiable energy appetite to brain-computer interfaces. From the question of which jobs disappear to concrete portfolios and an action plan for investors who want to act rather than watch.

This book ends with a personal confession. And a dedication to the author's grandchildren, for whom technology optimism isn't an abstract attitude — it's a necessity.

## About the Author
Thomas Huhn, born in 1963, has been working at the intersection of technology and entrepreneurship for over thirty years. After studying physics and business informatics, he got into the internet in 1994 — years before it went mainstream. He founded several technology companies and has been investing in cryptocurrencies and blockchain infrastructure since 2017.

His career has taught him to recognize technological disruptions early. And to have the courage to bet on them. In "The AI Species," he combines that experience with an investment thesis that connects three of the most powerful technology trends of our time.

Thomas Huhn lives at Starnberger See, south of Munich. He is the father of two daughters and grandfather to Mila and Malou, a dedicated gym athlete, and a music lover.

TheAiSpecies.world
